<user_id>117576855056664088520</user_id>< Name>
Michael Manguinao< /Name>
<Date>1498230701187< /Date>< Rating>
5< /Rating>
< Text>
A cozy, ethnic restaurant with delicious Cambodian food and superb dessert.

While you might just casually pass up this inconspicuous restaurant while walking along Broadway, you'd be playing yourself. The inside is cozy and inviting with all the Southeast Asian decor and friendly service.

The menu offers a variety of lunch and dinner specials, from salads to grilled items to curries. We got a rice crepe with chopped chicken to start and had a seafood medley curry and beef shish kabob with brown rice. Everything was savory, cooked perfectly, and delicious. The rice crepe, stuffed with bean sprouts and topped with a garlic vinegar sauce was surprisingly fresh and was a great way to start off the meal. The shish kabob was juicy and flavorful, and the curry was out of this world. The fish was buttery and tender, and curry matched perfectly with a side of rice.

The dessert here is so good, they have permanent dessert menus fixed under the glass of each table. We got the fried banana with house coconut ice cream, as well as the fresh manila mango with sticky rice. Both were satisfying without being overly sweet and a perfect way to end the meal.

I would highly recommend trying this place out!< /Text>

<user_id>115881395965102821695</user_id><Name>Evelyn Lindsey< /Name>< gmap_id>
0x808f80b6fbe64651:0xb3494c54f0db3e31<//gmap_id>
< Text>
Battambang was recommended by our foodie cousins and they weren't wrong. The food is familiar on one hand and slightly unusual on the other. Two of us shared the following: the Num Banchou which is a rice flour crepe stuffed with chicken, prawn, onion and sprouts: the Battambang noodles which is akin to Pad Thai (sorry for mixing cuisines) but satisfyingly rich with a tamarind sauce. But the most unexpected and wonderful dish was the Kdarm Salk Bam porng - soft shell crab in a sweet coconut sauce. Exquisite! I can't wait to initiate others to the wonderful world of Cambodian cuisine and look forward to working my way through the menu.<//Text>

<rating>5</rating><Text>Battambastic!!! This place was incredible. I wasn't sure what Cambodian food was like, but now I'm spoiled.

Upon many other E-recommendations I had the Grilled Lamb Chops with the side of sautÃ©ed veggies. The lamb was cooked perfectly and very flavorful.

The Battambang Noodles are similar to Pad Thai, which had a bit more flavor if you askes me. Very similar though with orangey noodles, peanuts, sprouts, and we went with chicken.

The little Lawt fried pork egg rolls went quick. So, you may need 2 orders.

We also shared some shrimp fried rice which was quickly devoured by my family of pirranahs.

Sodas come in their natural can, so you can count on what you're getting and for only $1.50.

All the way around Battambang was an absolute hit, and super welcoming staff too.< /Text>< pics>

< Text>
Went here on a weeknight and had a great meal. Very close to many downtown locations, including the convention center. The hosts were polite, funny, and incredibly informative about the (very) long menu. Many of the dishes have fish sauce in it, so if that smell upsets you may want to reconsider. The menu does have a few vegan options without fish sauce as well.

I recommend any of the appetizers with anchovy sauce, which was delicious. The catfish special was cooked perfectly and went along great with rice. One of the highlights of the meal was the young coconut drink which was incredibly fresh and had lots of tender coconut meat inside to share with the table.</Text>

< Review>
Great place to get shoes and insoles to support your feet. My wife just had a diagnose of neuroma condition. The doctor recommended to come to this store for an insole and a shoe.

This store has very highly tech equipment that would help you to measure the exact fitting of your feet. My wife got a 3D view of her feet on a platform and was fitted with a right sole to correct her feet condition.

With the computer rendering of fitting, the sales person was able to bring a few recommendations for shoes to go along with the insoles. After wearing those shoes, my wife felt the pain in her feet went away. Those high tech gadgets worked wonders.

They do have a lot of shoes and athletic apparels here for the New Balance brand. And I believe running shoes are very good as I was walking around browsing the displays while my wife was fitting her shoes.

The store allows only a couple of people in the store at a time and placed many covid safety measures. They do clean the machines between customers for fitting.

The parking lot is huge. It can probably accommodate over 50 cars. Thanks<//Review>

<Rate>4<//Rate>< review>
Great sandwich shop!

I'm a big fan of the sandwiches offered here. If you serve dutch crunch, I'll be there in a heartbeat. There are lots of interesting types of sandwich here and the menu seems to be slightly different every time. Regardless of the insides, always go for the dutch crunch. Extra crispy with a hint of sweetness. What's there not to love! The voodoo chips are pretty great too. I'm a fan of the spicy variety.

I think it's awesome that they give a lollipop with every meal. That's a sweet touch! Cheers.<//review>

< UserId.>
116174002019688720950< /UserId.>
< username>
cylarz< /username>
<Date>1405154439342<//Date><rating>5< /rating><Text>I've been a member here for a couple of years. Everyone here is very friendly and helpful. One range safety officer comes off as a bit of a drill sergeant, but he's actually a great guy if you take the time to get to know him. Likewise with the other range officers, and I always have a great time chatting with the other shooters during cease-fire too. Some will even let you shoot their weapons if you ask nicely.

Hands-down best value for the money of any range within an hour's drive of Sacramento. Only $10/head with no time limit - and if you join the Lincoln Rifle Club they allow you unlimited use of the facility for an entire year for only $60. Other local ranges charge $17/head or more, with only a small discount for members. There is no onsite retail store, but who needs that? Just go to Wal Mart for your supplies or to a specialty gun store before your shooting session.

Targets are clearly marked, and rules are strict but few. As long as you have your chamber flag in during cease fire (and then stay away from the bench while range is cold), don't rapid fire and don't draw from a holster, the staff won't bother you.

This place beats Spenceville hands-down. It's safe and controlled by comparison, has comfortable places to sit during both "range hot" and "range cold," and doesn't have garbage lying all over. It also beats several other area ranges on price, attitude, and range rules.

DO NOT argue with the range officers. They will kick you out if you're deemed a safety risk.< /Text>< Pictures>

They also have a bar and you can be seated in the bar to eat if you like but I wanted to sit in the dinning room all by myself. So I did.</Text>

< Rating>
3</Rating>
<review>Carl's Jr.'s menu holds very limited appeal to me. For food that is supposedly fast, I never seem to be able to get out of Carl's Jr. with my order in hand in any less than 15 minutes. Their lackluster burgers seemingly take just as long as Five Guys' or In-n-Out's to prepare, yet are significantly inferior in every way. The fries are a lame impression of McDonald's. Aside from the limited run of the "Babyback Rib Burger," I can't think of anything I've ever ordered for lunch or dinner at CJ's that I haven't immediately regretted. The aforementioned rib burger was like an upgraded McRib with crunchy onion straws but alas no longer available.

The breakfast menu at CJ's is somewhat better. I don't hate the "Sausage Egg and Cheese Biscuit." In fact, their biscuit may be the very best biscuit in fast food currently. The egg is a bit weird, like very thinly rendered egg that has the girth and lightness of a folded napkin. Also, like a lot of fast food "yellow egg product," the flavor is more aggressively "eggy" than you'd expect -- and certainly moreso than if you scrambled an egg at home. My solution? Order without the egg. You won't miss it.

This is a co-branded Green Burrito/Carl's Jr. restaurant. There exists approximately 300 of these co-branded Green Burrito/Carl's Jr. stores, almost exclusively in the western and southwestern United States. Despite being located in the middle of University City, this particular location's drive-thru intercom system is ghetto, ensuring you need to repeat your order fourteen times on average before the order-taker understands you. Other than that, I'd consider this to be an "average" Green Burrito/Carl's Jr. location.< /review><Pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOR7V3tAGC52QsOuVuom1w2ywkyP8Hn3L0EC9Ck=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNSL8HLbRg2VqusRxn-enTDezfBUIfaaMI-8usH=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pictures>< response>

< Review>
I've been to this Carl's Jr./Green Burrito several (20+) times and have been pretty disappointed by the service.

They have gotten my order wrong around 50% of the times I've been there. Sometimes it's just a minor mistake like forgetting to include the sauce. Sometimes they will give me the wrong items or completely forget to include items.

On top of that, for some reason the food at this particular location does not taste as good as other Carl's Jr. locations I've been to.

One good thing about this location is that the staff is usually very friendly. However, they seem to be understaffed often, which makes the drive-thru service very slow.

At least they are open 24 hours/day, which is very convenient as most nearby restaurants are closed late at night.< /Review>

I've been coming to this place virtually everyday for years and my experience with both staff and restaurant has been stellar.
